وقد اعتبر المحققون فيها سبعة قيود:
الأول: أن تكون قولاً أو فعلاً أو تركاً، فالأول كالقرآن، والثاني كنبع الماء من بين أصابعه، والثالث كعدم إحراق النار لسيدنا إبراهيم، وخرج بذلك الصفة القديمة، كما إذا قال: آيه صدقي كونُ الإلهِ متصفاً بصفة الاختراع.
الثاني: أن تكون خارقة للعادة، وهي ما اعتاده الناس واستمروا عليه مرةً بعد أخرى، وخرج بذلك غير الخارق، كما إذا قال: (آيةُ صدقي طلوع الشمس من حيث تطلع، وغروبها من حيث تغرب).
الثالث: أن تكون على يد مدعي النبوة أو الرسالة، وخرج بذلك الكرامة؛ وهي ما يظهر على يد عبد ظاهر الصلاح والمعونة: وهي ما يظهر على يد العوام تخليصاً لهم من شدة والاستدراج وهو ما يظهر على يد فاسق خديعة ومكراً به، والإهانة: وهي ما يظهر على يده تكذيباً له؛ كما وقع لمسيلمة الكذاب؛ فإنه تَفَلَ في عين أعور لتبرأ فعميت الصحيحة.
الرابع: أن تكون مقرونةً بدعوى النبوة أو الرسالة حقيقة أو حكماً بأن تأخرت بزمن يسير، وخرج بذلك الإرهاص؛ وهو ما كان قبل النبوة والرسالة تأسيساً لها، كإظلال الغمام له قبل البعثة.
الخامس: أن تكون موافقة للدعوى، وخرج بذلك المخالف لها، كما إذا قال: (آية صدقي انفلاق البحر فانفلق الجبل).
السادس: ألا تكون مكذبة له، وخرج بذلك ما إذا كانت مكذبة له، كما إذا قال: (آية صدقي نطقُ هذا الجماد فنطق بأنه مفتر كذاب، بخلاف ما لو قال: (آية صدقي نطق هذا الإنسان الميت وإحياؤه، فأحيي ونطق بأنه مفتر كذاب)، والفرق أن الجماد لا اختيار له فاعتبر تكذيبه؛ لأنه أمر إلهي، والإنسان مختار فلا يعتبر تكذيبه؛ لأنه ربما اختار الكفر على الإيمان.
السابع: أن تتعذر معارضته، وخرج بذلك السحر ومنه الشعبذة، في اليد يرى أن لها حقيقة ولا حقيقة لها كما يقع للحواة.
And the verifiers have considered in it seven restrictions: First: that it be a statement or an action or an omission, the first like the Quran, the second like the gushing of water from between his fingers, and the third like the fire not burning our master Abraham, and thereby the eternal attribute is excluded, as if he says: 'The sign of my truthfulness is that God is described with the attribute of invention.' Second: that it be a breach of custom, which is what people have become accustomed to and continued upon time after time, and thereby what is not a breach of custom is excluded, as if he says: 'The sign of my truthfulness is the rising of the sun from where it rises and its setting from where it sets.' Third: that it be at the hand of one claiming prophethood or messengershood, and thereby karamah is excluded; it is what appears at the hand of a servant outwardly righteous, and mu'awnah: it is what appears at the hand of common people to deliver them from hardship, and istidraj: it is what appears at the hand of a sinner as deception and trickery, and ihana: it is what appears at his hand as a denial of him; as occurred to Musaylimah the liar; for he spat into the eye of a one-eyed man to heal it, but the sound eye went blind. The Eighth Condition and Poetic Classification of Extraordinary Events
The author adds an eighth condition and presents a poetic classification of extraordinary events.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the eighth condition for miracles and be able to distinguish the six types of extraordinary events as classified by theologians.

Core Idea
Not every wonder is a miracle; extraordinary events are judged by their source and timing.

After discussing the general conditions for miracles, theologians added an important eighth condition: a miracle cannot occur during a time when the natural order is already broken, such as the Dajjal's era. The author then presents a poetic classification that organizes the entire range of extraordinary events—from prophetic miracles to the humiliations of liars—into six clear categories. This lesson will help you navigate these terms and understand their significance in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening condition
Read the first part of the passage where the eighth condition is stated. Notice how the Dajjal's acts are excluded because they happen during widespread abnormality.
The condition aims to prevent confusion between true miracles and events that occur in a context of general supernatural disruption.
2
Study the poem's categories
Read the poem and identify each of the six categories. For each, note the type of person involved and the technical term.
Use the translation to follow the rhyme scheme if helpful.
3
Explore the disputed category
The passage ends with a note that some add sorcery as a seventh category, but the correct view is that it is not extraordinary because it can be learned and repeated.
This reinforces the idea that extraordinary events must be 'beyond custom' in a permanent sense.
4
Reflect on the classification's purpose
Consider why kalam scholars invested effort in this taxonomy. How does it protect the uniqueness of prophetic miracles?
Think about common confusions between saintly karamah and prophetic mu'jizah.
5
Test your understanding
Attempt the checkpoint quiz at the end of the lesson to confirm you can match each term to its definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزاد بعضهم ثامناً: وهو ألا تكون في زمن نقض العادة؛ كزمن طلوع الشمس من مغربها، وخرج بذلك ما يقع من الدجال؛ كأمره للسماء أن تُمْطِرَ فَتُمْطِرُ، وللأرض أن تُنْبِتَ فتنبت. وقد نظم بعضهم أقسام الأمر الخارق للعادة، فقال: [من الطويل]
إذا ما رَأَيْتَ الأَمرَ يُحْرَقُ عَادة 	 فَمُعْجِزَةٌ إِنْ مِنْ نَبِيٍّ لَنا صَدَرٌ
وإِنْ بانَ مِنْهُ قَبْلَ وَصْفِ نُبُوَّةِ 	 فَالإِرْهَاصَ سَمِّهُ تَتَّبِعِ القَوْمَ فِي الْأَثَرُ
وإِنْ جَاءَ يَوماً مِنْ وَلِيٍّ فَإِنَّهُ الـ 	 كَرَامَةُ فِي التَّحْقِيقِ عِنْدَ ذَوِي النَّظَرْ
وإنْ كانَ مِنْ بَعضِ العَوامِ صُدُورُهُ 	 فَكَنَّوْهُ حَقًّا بالمَعُونَةِ وَاشْتَهَرْ
ومِن فَاسِقٍ إِنْ كانَ وَفْقَ مُرادِهِ 	 يُسَمَّى بِالِاسْتِدْرَاجِ فِيمَا قَدِ اسْتَقَرْ
وإِلَّا فَيُدْعَى بِالإِهانَةِ عِنْدَهُمْ 	 وقَدْ تَمَّتِ الأَقْسَامُ عِنْدَ الَّذِي اخْتَبَرْ
وزاد بعضهم السحر، وقيل: إنه ليس من الخوارق؛ لأنه معتاد عند تعاطي أسبابه.
And some added an eighth: that it not be in a time of the breaking of custom; like the time of the sun rising from its setting place, and thereby what occurs from the Dajjal is excluded; like his commanding the sky to rain and it rains, and the earth to grow and it grows. And some organized the categories of the extraordinary matter in verse, saying: [in the meter of tawil]
When you see an event that breaks custom, then it is a miracle if it comes from a prophet of ours.
And if it appears from him before the description of prophethood, then call it irhas; follow the people in the trace.
And if it comes one day from a saint, then it is karamah in verification with those of insight.
And if it occurs from some common people, then call it truly mu'awnah, and it is famous.
And from a sinner, if it is in accordance with his desire, it is called istidraj in what has been established.
And otherwise it is called ihana among them, and the categories are completed with the one who tested.
And some added sorcery, and it is said that it is not among the extraordinary because it is customary when its causes are practiced.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage contains two parts: an additional condition and a poetic classification.

First, an eighth condition is added: the miracle should not occur during a time when the natural order is already disrupted (e.g., the sun rising from the west). Such events would not serve as miracles because they occur in an already extraordinary context. The example given is the Dajjal's actions, which are not miracles because they happen during a time of widespread abnormality.

Second, a poetic summary organizes extraordinary events into six categories:
- Mu'jizah (miracle): from a prophet.
- Irhas (preparatory sign): before prophethood.
- Karamah (grace): from a saint.
- Mu'awnah (assistance): from common people in distress.
- Istidraj (gradual deception): from a sinner fulfilling his desire.
- Ihanah (humiliation): from a liar or imposter, like Musaylimah.
Finally, sorcery is mentioned as a disputed category: some include it as extraordinary, but the correct view is that it is not because it can be learned and repeated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All extraordinary events are miracles that prove prophethood.
Correction: Only mu'jizah from a prophet proves prophethood; other events like karamah or istidraj do not.

Checkpoint
According to the poem, what is the term for an extraordinary event that occurs from a saint?
A) Mu'jizah
B) Irhas
C) Karamah
D) Ihanah

Key Takeaway
Extraordinary events are not all miracles; they are classified by who performs them and when, with only the prophet's miracle serving as proof of prophethood.

The lesson teaches that from a sinner, if it fulfills his desire, it is called istidraj. Do you know the state of your own soul? Will you use this lesson to examine your actions and repent before that favor becomes a trap?
?
You may have heard stories of saints performing karamat. But this lesson demands that you check the source: if an extraordinary event comes from a person claiming prophethood, it must be a miracle. Are you too quick to accept any wonder-worker as a saint? The lesson gives clear categories. Will you apply them to discern truth from falsehood in the stories you hear?
?
The eighth condition warns that events during the Dajjal's time will not be miracles. The Dajjal is yet to come, but the lesson challenges you: are you so attached to the normal course of life that you would be deceived by his wonders? What is your anchor? This lesson reminds us that the only true miracle is the one that comes with a claim of prophethood and is inimitable. Will you strengthen your knowledge of the Prophet's ﷺ miracles so you are not swayed by any other?

The Doctrine of Prophetic Infallibility (Ismah)
Explanation of prophetic infallibility and its proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari doctrine of prophetic infallibility: that prophets are protected from both major and minor sins, the debate about forgetfulness, and that the basis for this knowledge is revelation.

Core Idea
Prophets are protected from all sins—major and minor—by divine safeguard.

The inviolability of prophets (ismah) is a core belief in Islamic theology. This lesson explores the definition, the scholarly consensus on the extent of this protection, and the epistemological basis for knowing it. The passage from Tuhfat al-Murid explains the correct view and cites key authorities.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and its translation
Begin by reading the source text and its literal translation. Notice the grammatical comment about 'ismah attributed to God as the protector.
The passage opens with a line from the poem, which the commentary explains.
2
Identify the key claims about ismah
Look for three claims: (1) prophets are protected from minor sins like major sins; (2) the chosen view is protection from both; (3) the source of knowledge is revelation (sam‘) according to Ash‘aris, but reason according to Mu‘tazilites.
3
Compare the differing scholarly opinions
Note that al-Razi distinguished between intentional sins (protected) and forgetfulness (permitted), while the majority held protection from both. Also note the epistemological disagreement with the Mu‘tazilites.
This step helps understand the range of views within the tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وَعِصْمَةَ البارِي لِكُلِّ حَنْمَا): الإضافة في (عصمة الباري) من إضافة المفعول إلى الفاعل، أي: عصمته الباري. وعصمة الأنبياء من الصغائر كعصمتهم من الكبائر على الصحيح، قال في «البحر المحيط»: والمختار امتناع ذلك، وأنهم معصومون من الصغائر والكبائر جميعاً، وعليه الأستاذ وابن فورك وأبو بكر بن مجاهد، واختار الرازي العصمة عمداً وجوزها سهواً. قال الآمدي في «إحكام الأحكام»: مدرك العصمة السمع كما ذهب إليه القاضي والمحققون من أصحابنا، أو العقل كما ذهب إليه المعتزلة.
His saying: 'And the inviolability of the Creator for every prophet' — the annexation in 'inviolability of the Creator' is of the object to the subject, i.e., the Creator's protection of him. And the inviolability of prophets from minor sins is like their inviolability from major sins according to the correct view. He said in 'al-Bahr al-Muhit': The chosen view is the impossibility of that, and that they are protected from minor and major sins altogether, and upon this are al-Ustadh, Ibn Furak, and Abu Bakr ibn Mujahid, and al-Razi chose inviolability from intentional sins and permitted it from forgetfulness. Al-Amidi said in 'Ihkam al-Ahkam': The epistemological source of inviolability is revelation, as al-Qadi and the verifiers among our companions held, or reason, as the Mu'tazilites held.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage explains the doctrine of prophetic infallibility (ismah). It begins by explaining a line from the poem: 'Wa 'ismata al-Bari li kulli hanma' — here 'ismah is attributed to God as the protector. The author then states the predominant view: prophets are protected from both minor and major sins, whether intentional or unintentional (with a difference regarding forgetfulness). He cites various authorities: the view in 'al-Bahr al-Muhit' that they are protected from all sins, supported by al-Ustadh, Ibn Furak, and Abu Bakr ibn Mujahid. Al-Razi differed by distinguishing intentional sins (protected) from sins of forgetfulness (permitted). He also cites al-Amidi on the source of knowledge of ismah: the Ash'ari school says it is known through revelation (sam'), while the Mu'tazilites say it is known through reason ('aql).

Key Terms
العصمة
الصغائر
الكبائر
السمع
العقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophets could commit minor sins because they are human.
Correction: The correct view is that prophets are protected from both major and minor sins; only al-Razi allowed forgetfulness.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the predominant view regarding prophets committing minor sins?
A) They are protected from major sins but not minor
B) They are protected from both minor and major sins
C) They are protected from sins done intentionally but not forgetfully
D) They are not protected from any sins

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari doctrine holds prophets infallible in both minor and major sins, with the basis in revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you rely more on revelation or your own reason when deciding right from wrong? What would change if you submitted your moral judgments entirely to the Qur'an and Sunnah?
?
The prophets were divinely protected from sin. What persistent sin do you need Allah's protection from right now? Have you sincerely begged Him to guard you from it?
?
Why do you think the Ash'aris insisted that prophetic infallibility is known through revelation and not reason? Could your own trust in revelation be shaken if you encounter something that seems 'unreasonable'?

Conditions of a True Miracle: Inimitability and Timing
Commentator lists two conditions for miracles and exclusion of magic and Dajjal events

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the seventh and eighth conditions of a true miracle and how they exclude magic and events occurring during times of broken custom.

Core Idea
A true miracle cannot be imitated and must occur in a time of normal custom.

Before declaring an event a miracle, theologians set strict conditions to distinguish divine acts from deception or mere coincidence. This passage presents two such conditions: the inability of others to replicate it, and its occurrence within the normal course of nature. These guard against confusion with magic or end-of-time events.

Guided Path
1
Read the seventh condition
Notice that the condition requires that no one can oppose or imitate the miracle. This excludes magic and sleight-of-hand.
Magic is habitual for practitioners, so it is not truly extraordinary.
2
Understand why magic is excluded
Magic and sleight-of-hand appear real but have no true reality, as in snake-charming. They can be imitated, so they are not miracles.
3
Learn the eighth condition
Some scholars added that the miracle must not occur in a time when the laws of nature are broken, like the rising of the sun from the west on Judgment Day.
This excludes events from the Dajjal (Antichrist) because they happen in such a time.
4
Summarize the exclusion
Both conditions serve to protect the definition of miracle from being applied to deceptive or eschatological events.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السابع: أن تتعذر معارضته، وخرج بذلك السحر ومنه الشعبذة، في اليد يرى أن لها حقيقة ولا حقيقة لها كما يقع للحواة. وزاد بعضهم ثامناً: وهو ألا تكون في زمن نقض العادة؛ كزمن طلوع الشمس من مغربها، وخرج بذلك ما يقع من الدجال؛ كأمره للسماء أن تُمْطِرَ فَتُمْطِرُ، وللأرض أن تُنْبِتَ فتنبت، وقد نظم بعضهم أقسام الأمر الخارق للعادة، فقال: [من الطويل] إذا ما رَأَيْتَ الأَمرَ يُحْرَقُ عَادة فَمُعْجِزَةٌ إِنْ مِنْ نَبِيٍّ لَنا صَدَرٌ وإِنْ بانَ مِنْهُ قَبْلَ وَصْفِ نُبُوَّةِ فَالإِرْهَاصَ سَمِّهُ تَتَّبِعِ القَوْمَ فِي الْأَثَرُ وإِنْ جَاءَ يَوماً مِنْ وَلِيٍّ فَإِنَّهُ الـ كَرَامَةُ فِي التَّحْقِيقِ عِنْدَ ذَوِي النَّظَرْ وإنْ كانَ مِنْ بَعضِ العَوامِ صُدُورُهُ فَكَنَّوْهُ حَقًّا بالمَعُونَةِ وَاشْتَهَرْ ومِن فَاسِقٍ إِنْ كانَ وَفْقَ مُرادِهِ يُسَمَّى بِالِاسْتِدْرَاجِ فِيمَا قَدِ اسْتَقَرْ وإِلَّا فَيُدْعَى بِالإِهانَةِ عِنْدَهُمْ وقَدْ تَمَّتِ الأَقْسَامُ عِنْدَ الَّذِي اخْتَبَرْ وزاد بعضهم السحر، وقيل: إنه ليس من الخوارق؛ لأنه معتاد عند تعاطي أسبابه.
Seventh: that its opposition be impossible, and by that magic is excluded, and from it is sleight-of-hand, in which the hand is seen to have a reality but has no reality, as occurs with snake-charmers. And some added an eighth: that it not be in a time of breaking of custom, like the time of the sun rising from its west, and by that what occurs from the Dajjal is excluded, like his commanding the sky to rain and it rains, and the earth to sprout and it sprouts. And some composed the divisions of the matter that breaks custom, saying: [al-tawil] When you see a matter that breaks custom, then it is a miracle if it issues from a prophet of ours. And if it appears from him before the description of prophethood, then call it irhas (preparatory miracle), following the people in the tradition. And if it comes one day from a saint, then it is karama (grace) in verification according to the people of insight. And if it issues from some commoners, then name it rightly ma'una (assistance), and it is well-known. And from a sinner, if it matches his desire, it is called istidraj (gradual entrapment) in what has been established. Otherwise, it is called ihana (disgrace) with them. And the divisions have been completed according to the one who tested. And some added magic, and it was said: it is not from the extraordinary, because it is habitual when its causes are practiced.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage defines and classifies extraordinary events (al-amr al-khariq li'l-ada). It begins by listing the seventh condition for a true miracle: that it cannot be opposed or imitated by anyone. This excludes magic and sleight-of-hand, which are imitable and lack true reality. Then an eighth condition is added: the miracle must not occur in a time when the normal course of nature is broken, such as the time when the sun will rise from the west, which is a sign of the last day. Events from the Dajjal (Antichrist) are excluded because they occur in such a time. Next, the commentator presents a poem that systematically enumerates the types of extraordinary events based on the status of the person from whom they originate: If from a prophet, it is a mu'jiza (miracle). If from someone before he becomes a prophet, it is irhas (preparatory miracle). If from a saint (wali), it is karama (grace). If from a common believer, it is ma'una (divine assistance). If from a sinner, and it matches his desire, it is istidraj (gradual entrapment leading to punishment). If from a sinner and it does not match his desire, it is ihana (disgrace). Some add magic, but it is not considered truly extraordinary because it is habitual for those who practice its causes.

Key Terms
معجزة
سحر
شعبذة
خارق للعادة
استدراج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Magic is a type of miracle.
Correction: Magic is not a miracle because it is imitable and habitual for those who practice it. A miracle must be inimitable.

Checkpoint
What is the seventh condition of a true miracle according to the passage?
A) It must be performed by a prophet
B) It must be impossible to oppose or imitate
C) It must occur during a time of broken custom
D) It must involve the Dajjal

Key Takeaway
A true miracle must be both inimitable and occur within the normal course of nature, excluding magic and end-time phenomena.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that a true miracle must be inimitable and occur within normal nature. Is your faith grounded in the clear, inimitable miracle of the Qur'an, or are you attracted to sensational signs and stories that could be imitated or occur in times of fitna? What will you do this week to strengthen your connection to the Qur'an as the ultimate miracle?
?
If the Dajjal were to appear today and perform his wonders, would you be deceived? How does the knowledge that his actions occur in a time of broken custom help you prepare your heart now? Examine your life: what steps have you taken to anchor your iman in sound proofs rather than extraordinary experiences?
?
Think of a time when you were impressed by someone's seemingly supernatural ability. How would you test that event against the two conditions from this lesson? Are you willing to admit that you might have been deceived by something imitable or poorly timed? Commit to using this criterion before accepting any claim of miracles.

Classification of Extraordinary Events
Poem enumerating six types of extraordinary events and discussion of magic

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the six types of extraordinary events based on the status of the person from whom they originate, as outlined in the poem.

Core Idea
Extraordinary events are classified by their source: prophets, saints, commoners, or sinners.

Not all extraordinary acts are miracles. Theologians have systematically categorized such events based on the doer. This passage presents a poetic enumeration of six types, from miracles to disgrace, and briefly addresses the status of magic. Understanding this classification helps avoid confusion when evaluating claims of supernatural occurrences.

Guided Path
1
Read the poem
The poem lists six types of extraordinary events. Read it through once, then use the commentary to understand each type.
The poem is in the meter al-tawil.
2
Identify the six types
They are: mu'jiza (prophet's miracle), irhas (pre-prophetic miracle), karama (saint's grace), ma'una (commoner's assistance), istidraj (sinner's entrapment), and ihana (sinner's disgrace).
These are all extraordinary, but their nature differs based on the person.
3
Understand the basis of classification
The key factor is the religious status of the person: prophet, saint, common believer, or sinner. The same act can be named differently depending on who does it.
4
Note the discussion on magic
Some scholars consider magic an extraordinary event, but others reject it because it is habitual when its causes are practiced.
Magic is not truly extraordinary in the theological sense.
5
Memorize the classifications
Using the poem as a mnemonic, you can recall each type and its associated person.
This classification is foundational in kalam for discussing prophethood and miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السابع: أن تتعذر معارضته، وخرج بذلك السحر ومنه الشعبذة، في اليد يرى أن لها حقيقة ولا حقيقة لها كما يقع للحواة. وزاد بعضهم ثامناً: وهو ألا تكون في زمن نقض العادة؛ كزمن طلوع الشمس من مغربها، وخرج بذلك ما يقع من الدجال؛ كأمره للسماء أن تُمْطِرَ فَتُمْطِرُ، وللأرض أن تُنْبِتَ فتنبت، وقد نظم بعضهم أقسام الأمر الخارق للعادة، فقال: [من الطويل] إذا ما رَأَيْتَ الأَمرَ يُحْرَقُ عَادة فَمُعْجِزَةٌ إِنْ مِنْ نَبِيٍّ لَنا صَدَرٌ وإِنْ بانَ مِنْهُ قَبْلَ وَصْفِ نُبُوَّةِ فَالإِرْهَاصَ سَمِّهُ تَتَّبِعِ القَوْمَ فِي الْأَثَرُ وإِنْ جَاءَ يَوماً مِنْ وَلِيٍّ فَإِنَّهُ الـ كَرَامَةُ فِي التَّحْقِيقِ عِنْدَ ذَوِي النَّظَرْ وإنْ كانَ مِنْ بَعضِ العَوامِ صُدُورُهُ فَكَنَّوْهُ حَقًّا بالمَعُونَةِ وَاشْتَهَرْ ومِن فَاسِقٍ إِنْ كانَ وَفْقَ مُرادِهِ يُسَمَّى بِالِاسْتِدْرَاجِ فِيمَا قَدِ اسْتَقَرْ وإِلَّا فَيُدْعَى بِالإِهانَةِ عِنْدَهُمْ وقَدْ تَمَّتِ الأَقْسَامُ عِنْدَ الَّذِي اخْتَبَرْ وزاد بعضهم السحر، وقيل: إنه ليس من الخوارق؛ لأنه معتاد عند تعاطي أسبابه.

The Obligation of 'Isma for Prophets and Angels
Commentator explains the grammatical and theological affirmation of 'isma for prophets and angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that 'isma (infallibility) is an obligatory divine protection for every prophet and angel, and how the grammatical structure of the text affirms this.

Core Idea
'Isma is a divine necessity that cannot be removed for any prophet or angel.

This lesson unpacks the commentator's explanation of the opening line of the section. He examines two possible grammatical readings of the word 'hatma' and concludes that both affirm the same theological truth: God's infallibility for prophets and angels is necessarily binding and permanent. He also addresses why the topic is repeated after trustworthiness.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the passage from the beginning down to the phrase 'wa la taqbal al-intifa''. Pay attention to the grammatical analysis.
The passage is dense; don't worry about every detail initially.
2
Understand the two readings of 'hatma'
The commentator explains two possible readings: one as an imperative verb (hatma) and one as a passive past verb (hutima). Both result in the same theological meaning.
The imperative reading is more common in the text.
3
Grasp the core meaning
The key sentence is: 'Believe that the infallibility of the Creator for every one of the prophets and angels is necessarily binding and obligatory; meaning that it is not separated and does not accept removal.'
This is the main doctrinal point.
4
See the inclusion of angels
The commentator notes that the reason for repeating 'isma after trustworthiness is to include angels in the same ruling.
Angels share in the obligation of 'isma with prophets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوب العصمة للأنبياء والرسل قوله : (وَعِصْمَةَ البارِي لِكُلِّ حَنْمَا ) : الإضافة في عصمة الباري) من إضافة منقلبة. المصدر لفاعله و(لكل) متعلّق بعصمة، و(حتما) بفتح الحاء على أنه فعل أمر، وألفه عن تون التوكيد الخفيفة في الوقف بعد حذف الرابط، والأصل: حتمنها، والجملة خبر المبتدأ ، وهو (عصمة إن قرئ بالرفع، ويصح أن يقرأ بالنصب على أنه مفعول لمحذوف يدلُّ عليه المذكور والتقدير وحتم عصمة الباري، ولم يجعل مفعولاً للمذكور؛ لأنه مقترن بنون التوكيد الخفيفة، وهو حينئذ لا يعمل فيما قبله . فإن قيل : إذا لم يعمل لا يفسر عاملاً أجيب بأن قولهم: (ما لا يعمل لا يفسر عاملاً) إنما هو في التفسير الاصطلاحي، فلا ينافي أنه يشير له في الجملة، أو بضم الحاء على أنه فعل ماض مبني للمجهول وألفه للإطلاق، وعلى هذا فـ (عصمة) بالرفع لا غير على أنه مبتدأ والجملة من الفعل ونائب الفاعل خبره وتذكير الضمير الذي هو نائب الفاعل مع كونه عائداً على العصمة لتذكيرها باعتبار كونها وصفاً، وعلى كل فالمعنى: اعتقد أن عصمة الباري لكلِّ واحدٍ من الأنبياء والملائكة متحتمة وواجبة؛ بمعنى أنها لا تنفك ولا تقبل الانتفاء، والباري) الخالق من البرء وهو الخلق، وقد يقال : إن عصمة الأنبياء قد تقدمت في قوله : ( وواجب) في حقهم الأمانة)؛ إذ الأمانة العصمة، وقد يُجاب بأنه إنما تعرّض لها ليجمع الملائكة مع الأنبياء في هي حكمها والاتصاف بها والعصمة لغةً مطلق الحفظ واصطلاحاً: حفظ الله للمكلف من الذنب مع استحالة وقوعه ولا يجوز لنا سؤال العصمة بهذا المعنى؛ كأن يقال: (اللهم إنا نسألك العصمة)، فإن أريد المعنى اللغوي جاز لنا سؤالها . واعلم أن المشهور عصمة جميع الملائكة، وقولهم : أَتَجْعَلُ فِيهَا مَن يُفْسِدُ فِيهَا وَيَسْفِكُ الدِّمَاءَ﴾ [البَقَرَة : ٣٠] ليس غيبةٌ ولا اعتراضاً على الله، بل مجرد استفهام، وما نقل في قصة هاروت وماروت مما يذكره المؤرخون لم يصح فيه شيء من الأخبار، بل هو من افتراء اليهود وكذبهم وتبعهم المؤرخون في ذكر ذلك، وقيل: كانا رجلين صالحين، وسُميا ملكين تشبيهاً لهما بالملكين. وأثبت الزمخشري العصمة للسيدة مريم في كشافه
The obligation of infallibility for the prophets and messengers. His saying: 'And the infallibility of the Creator for every one is necessarily binding': The genitive construction in 'infallibility of the Creator' is a reversed genitive. The verbal noun is for its subject, and 'for every' is attached to 'infallibility', and 'necessarily binding' (hatma) with a fatha on the ha' is a verb in the imperative, its alif replaces the nun of light emphasis in pausa after deleting the connector, and the original is 'hutimnaha', and the sentence is the predicate of the subject, which is 'infallibility' if read in the nominative, and it is permissible to read it in the accusative as an object of an omitted verb indicated by what is mentioned, the estimation being 'and the Creator necessarily bound infallibility', and it is not made the object of the mentioned verb because it is associated with the light nun of emphasis, and then it does not operate on what is before it. If it is said: Since it does not operate, it does not govern a factor, it is answered that their saying: 'What does not operate does not govern a factor' is only in technical interpretation, so it does not contradict that it indicates it in the sentence, or with a damma on the ha' as a passive past verb with its alif for absolute, and on this 'infallibility' is nominative only as a subject and the sentence of the verb and its deputy is its predicate, and the masculinization of the pronoun which is the deputy despite its referring to infallibility due to its feminization by considering it a description. In any case, the meaning is: Believe that the infallibility of the Creator for every one of the prophets and angels is necessarily binding and obligatory, meaning that it is not separated and does not accept removal. And 'the Creator' (al-Bari) is the Creator from al-bar' which is creation. And it may be said: The infallibility of the prophets has already preceded in His saying: 'And obligatory upon them is trustworthiness', since trustworthiness is infallibility. And it may be answered that he only brought it up to include the angels with the prophets in its ruling and description. And infallibility linguistically is absolute protection, and terminologically: God's protection of the morally responsible person from sin with the impossibility of its occurrence, and it is not permissible for us to ask for infallibility in this sense, such as saying: 'O God, we ask You for infallibility', but if the linguistic meaning is intended, it is permissible for us to ask for it. And know that the well-known view is the infallibility of all angels. And their saying: 'Will You place therein one who causes corruption therein and sheds blood?' [Al-Baqarah 2:30] is neither backbiting nor an objection to God, but merely a question. And what has been narrated in the story of Harut and Marut that historians mention, none of the reports is authentic, rather it is from the fabrication of the Jews and their lies, and the historians followed them in mentioning that. And it was said: They were two righteous men, and they were called angels by way of comparison to the two angels. And al-Zamakhshari affirmed the infallibility of Lady Maryam in his Kashshaf.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage is a theological and grammatical explanation of the line 'And the infallibility of the Creator for every one is necessarily binding' from the Jawharat al-Tawhid. The commentator begins by noting that the obligation of 'isma (infallibility) for prophets and messengers is being discussed. He provides a detailed grammatical analysis of the line, considering two possible readings for 'hatma': as an imperative verb meaning 'necessarily bind' or as a passive verb meaning 'was necessarily bound'. Both readings affirm that God's infallibility for prophets and angels is obligatory and cannot be removed. The commentator then addresses a potential redundancy: since trustworthiness (amana) was already mentioned as obligatory for prophets, why is 'isma repeated? The answer is to include angels in the same ruling. Next, he defines 'isma linguistically as absolute protection and terminologically as God's protection of the morally responsible person from sin with the impossibility of its occurrence. He distinguishes between asking for 'isma in the technical sense (which is not permissible) and in the linguistic sense (which is permissible). Finally, he affirms the well-known view that all angels are infallible, clarifies that the angels' question in the Quran is not an objection, and refutes the story of Harut and Marut as fabricated, suggesting they were righteous men metaphorically called angels. He notes that al-Zamakhshari affirmed Mary's infallibility.

Key Terms
وجوب العصمة
عصمة
حتما

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'isma applies only to prophets and not to angels.
Correction: The text explicitly includes angels: 'for every one of the prophets and angels'.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what do both grammatical readings of 'hatma' affirm?
A) That 'isma is optional for prophets
B) That 'isma is necessarily binding and permanent
C) That 'isma applies only to angels
D) That 'isma can be removed under certain conditions

Key Takeaway
'Isma is an obligatory and permanent divine protection for every prophet and angel.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on the fact that God's protection for the prophets and angels is 'necessarily binding and does not accept removal', does your heart feel secure in their guidance, or do you find yourself skeptical about their perfection? What does that reveal about your own trust in God's wisdom?
?
The commentator mentions that the repetition of 'isma serves to include angels with prophets. Have you ever considered the angels' absolute obedience and protection? How does this reality challenge your own excuses for disobedience? Will you today seek to align your actions with that same level of devotion, even if you are not protected by 'isma yourself?
?
If you truly internalize that 'isma is a divine necessity, it means no prophet ever made a mistake in conveying the message. Does this increase your reliance on their teachings? Or are there areas where you still doubt their infallibility? Confess that to yourself and commit to removing that doubt.

The Definition of 'Isma and Asking for It
Commentator defines 'isma and distinguishes between linguistic and technical senses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic and technical definitions of 'isma and the ruling on asking God for 'isma.

Core Idea
'Isma in the technical sense is not to be asked for, only in the linguistic sense.

The commentator defines 'isma both linguistically and technically. He then clarifies a common misunderstanding: while we cannot ask for 'isma in the technical sense (since it implies impossibility of sin), we may ask for protection (linguistic sense).

Guided Path
1
Read the definition passage
Read the Arabic text defining 'isma linguistically and technically.
The definition is compact but clear.
2
Distinguish the two definitions
Linguistically, 'isma is simply 'absolute protection'. Technically, it is 'God's protection of the morally responsible person from sin with the impossibility of its occurrence'.
The technical sense adds the impossibility of sin.
3
Understand the ruling on asking
We cannot ask for 'isma in the technical sense because that would be asking for impossibility of sin, which is a divine prerogative. However, we can ask for protection in the linguistic sense.
The example given is saying 'O God, we ask You for 'isma' – this is permissible only if intending the linguistic meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوب العصمة للأنبياء والرسل قوله : (وَعِصْمَةَ البارِي لِكُلِّ حَنْمَا ) : الإضافة في عصمة الباري) من إضافة منقلبة. المصدر لفاعله و(لكل) متعلّق بعصمة، و(حتما) بفتح الحاء على أنه فعل أمر، وألفه عن تون التوكيد الخفيفة في الوقف بعد حذف الرابط، والأصل: حتمنها، والجملة خبر المبتدأ ، وهو (عصمة إن قرئ بالرفع، ويصح أن يقرأ بالنصب على أنه مفعول لمحذوف يدلُّ عليه المذكور والتقدير وحتم عصمة الباري، ولم يجعل مفعولاً للمذكور؛ لأنه مقترن بنون التوكيد الخفيفة، وهو حينئذ لا يعمل فيما قبله . فإن قيل : إذا لم يعمل لا يفسر عاملاً أجيب بأن قولهم: (ما لا يعمل لا يفسر عاملاً) إنما هو في التفسير الاصطلاحي، فلا ينافي أنه يشير له في الجملة، أو بضم الحاء على أنه فعل ماض مبني للمجهول وألفه للإطلاق، وعلى هذا فـ (عصمة) بالرفع لا غير على أنه مبتدأ والجملة من الفعل ونائب الفاعل خبره وتذكير الضمير الذي هو نائب الفاعل مع كونه عائداً على العصمة لتذكيرها باعتبار كونها وصفاً، وعلى كل فالمعنى: اعتقد أن عصمة الباري لكلِّ واحدٍ من الأنبياء والملائكة متحتمة وواجبة؛ بمعنى أنها لا تنفك ولا تقبل الانتفاء، والباري) الخالق من البرء وهو الخلق، وقد يقال : إن عصمة الأنبياء قد تقدمت في قوله : ( وواجب) في حقهم الأمانة)؛ إذ الأمانة العصمة، وقد يُجاب بأنه إنما تعرّض لها ليجمع الملائكة مع الأنبياء في هي حكمها والاتصاف بها والعصمة لغةً مطلق الحفظ واصطلاحاً: حفظ الله للمكلف من الذنب مع استحالة وقوعه ولا يجوز لنا سؤال العصمة بهذا المعنى؛ كأن يقال: (اللهم إنا نسألك العصمة)، فإن أريد المعنى اللغوي جاز لنا سؤالها . واعلم أن المشهور عصمة جميع الملائكة، وقولهم : أَتَجْعَلُ فِيهَا مَن يُفْسِدُ فِيهَا وَيَسْفِكُ الدِّمَاءَ﴾ [البَقَرَة : ٣٠] ليس غيبةٌ ولا اعتراضاً على الله، بل مجرد استفهام، وما نقل في قصة هاروت وماروت مما يذكره المؤرخون لم يصح فيه شيء من الأخبار، بل هو من افتراء اليهود وكذبهم وتبعهم المؤرخون في ذكر ذلك، وقيل: كانا رجلين صالحين، وسُميا ملكين تشبيهاً لهما بالملكين. وأثبت الزمخشري العصمة للسيدة مريم في كشافه
The obligation of infallibility for the prophets and messengers. His saying: 'And the infallibility of the Creator for every one is necessarily binding': The genitive construction in 'infallibility of the Creator' is a reversed genitive. The verbal noun is for its subject, and 'for every' is attached to 'infallibility', and 'necessarily binding' (hatma) with a fatha on the ha' is a verb in the imperative, its alif replaces the nun of light emphasis in pausa after deleting the connector, and the original is 'hutimnaha', and the sentence is the predicate of the subject, which is 'infallibility' if read in the nominative, and it is permissible to read it in the accusative as an object of an omitted verb indicated by what is mentioned, the estimation being 'and the Creator necessarily bound infallibility', and it is not made the object of the mentioned verb because it is associated with the light nun of emphasis, and then it does not operate on what is before it. If it is said: Since it does not operate, it does not govern a factor, it is answered that their saying: 'What does not operate does not govern a factor' is only in technical interpretation, so it does not contradict that it indicates it in the sentence, or with a damma on the ha' as a passive past verb with its alif for absolute, and on this 'infallibility' is nominative only as a subject and the sentence of the verb and its deputy is its predicate, and the masculinization of the pronoun which is the deputy despite its referring to infallibility due to its feminization by considering it a description. In any case, the meaning is: Believe that the infallibility of the Creator for every one of the prophets and angels is necessarily binding and obligatory, meaning that it is not separated and does not accept removal. And 'the Creator' (al-Bari) is the Creator from al-bar' which is creation. And it may be said: The infallibility of the prophets has already preceded in His saying: 'And obligatory upon them is trustworthiness', since trustworthiness is infallibility. And it may be answered that he only brought it up to include the angels with the prophets in its ruling and description. And infallibility linguistically is absolute protection, and terminologically: God's protection of the morally responsible person from sin with the impossibility of its occurrence, and it is not permissible for us to ask for infallibility in this sense, such as saying: 'O God, we ask You for infallibility', but if the linguistic meaning is intended, it is permissible for us to ask for it. And know that the well-known view is the infallibility of all angels. And their saying: 'Will You place therein one who causes corruption therein and sheds blood?' [Al-Baqarah 2:30] is neither backbiting nor an objection to God, but merely a question. And what has been narrated in the story of Harut and Marut that historians mention, none of the reports is authentic, rather it is from the fabrication of the Jews and their lies, and the historians followed them in mentioning that. And it was said: They were two righteous men, and they were called angels by way of comparison to the two angels. And al-Zamakhshari affirmed the infallibility of Lady Maryam in his Kashshaf.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage is a theological and grammatical explanation of the line 'And the infallibility of the Creator for every one is necessarily binding' from the Jawharat al-Tawhid. The commentator begins by noting that the obligation of 'isma (infallibility) for prophets and messengers is being discussed. He provides a detailed grammatical analysis of the line, considering two possible readings for 'hatma': as an imperative verb meaning 'necessarily bind' or as a passive verb meaning 'was necessarily bound'. Both readings affirm that God's infallibility for prophets and angels is obligatory and cannot be removed. The commentator then addresses a potential redundancy: since trustworthiness (amana) was already mentioned as obligatory for prophets, why is 'isma repeated? The answer is to include angels in the same ruling. Next, he defines 'isma linguistically as absolute protection and terminologically as God's protection of the morally responsible person from sin with the impossibility of its occurrence. He distinguishes between asking for 'isma in the technical sense (which is not permissible) and in the linguistic sense (which is permissible). Finally, he affirms the well-known view that all angels are infallible, clarifies that the angels' question in the Quran is not an objection, and refutes the story of Harut and Marut as fabricated, suggesting they were righteous men metaphorically called angels. He notes that al-Zamakhshari affirmed Mary's infallibility.

Key Terms
عصمة
العصمة لغة
العصمة اصطلاحا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is permissible to ask God for 'isma in the technical sense (i.e., to be made infallible like prophets).
Correction: The commentator states it is not permissible to ask for 'isma in the technical sense; only the linguistic sense of protection may be requested.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, when is it permissible to ask God for 'isma?
A) Only in the technical sense
B) Only in the linguistic sense
C) In both senses
D) In neither sense

Key Takeaway
'Isma in its technical sense is not to be asked for; only the linguistic sense of protection may be requested.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite du‘as like 'Allāhumma innā nas'aluka al-‘iṣmah', have you ever reflected on what you are actually asking for? After learning that technical ‘iṣmah entails the impossibility of sin, will you change your supplication to align with the permissible linguistic meaning? Commit to revising your du‘a tonight.
?
The lesson teaches that technical ‘iṣmah is not to be asked for because it is impossible for most people. Does this reality humble you or frustrate you? How does knowing that you are not ma‘ṣūm affect your approach to tawbah and your reliance on Allah’s mercy? Write down one specific sin you will actively strive against this week, acknowledging your lack of ismah.
?
The passage distinguishes between two meanings of the same word. Are there other Islamic terms you have been using without distinguishing their linguistic and technical senses? Reflect on a term like 'rahman' or 'iman'. How might this oversight affect your understanding of Allah’s attributes or your own iman? Identify one term to study more deeply this month.

The Infallibility of Angels and Refutation of False Narratives
Commentator discusses angelic infallibility and refutes false narratives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the well-known view that all angels are infallible, the correct interpretation of the angels' question in the Quran, and the refutation of the Harut and Marut story.

Core Idea
Angels are all infallible; stories contradicting this are fabrications.

This lesson covers the commentator's affirmation that all angels are infallible. He explains that the angels' question in Surah Al-Baqarah is not an objection but a query. He then refutes the fabricated story of Harut and Marut, noting that it originates from Jewish falsehoods, and mentions that al-Zamakhshari affirmed Mary's infallibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on angels
Read the Arabic text from 'wa'lam anna al-mashhur' to the end.
This passage deals with angelic infallibility and related issues.
2
Understand the infallibility of all angels
The commentator states the well-known view (mashhur) that all angels are infallible. This means they cannot commit sins.
This is a consensus among Sunni scholars.
3
Interpret the angels' question in Quran 2:30
The angels' statement 'Will You place therein one who causes corruption...' is not backbiting or an objection, but a mere question seeking wisdom.
Angels do not object to God's decree.
4
Refute the Harut and Marut story
The story of Harut and Marut as angels who sinned is not authentic; it is from Jewish fabrications. Some say they were righteous men called angels metaphorically.
The commentator affirms no authentic narration supports their sin.
5
Note on Maryam's infallibility
Al-Zamakhshari affirmed the infallibility of Lady Maryam in his tafsir.
This is a related point from another scholar.

His saying: 'And the infallibility of the Creator for every one is necessarily binding': The genitive construction in 'infallibility of the Creator' is a reversed genitive. The verbal noun is for its subject, and 'for every' is attached to 'infallibility', and 'necessarily binding' (hatma) with a fatha on the ha' is a verb in the imperative, its alif replaces the nun of light emphasis in pausa after deleting the connector, and the original is 'hutimnaha', and the sentence is the predicate of the subject, which is 'infallibility' if read in the nominative, and it is permissible to read it in the accusative as an object of an omitted verb indicated by what is mentioned, the estimation being 'and the Creator necessarily bound infallibility', and it is not made the object of the mentioned verb because it is associated with the light nun of emphasis, and then it does not operate on what is before it. How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This lesson teaches that the angels' question was not an objection but a sincere inquiry. Think of a recent situation where you assumed someone's words were a complaint or criticism. Could it have been a genuine question? Will you give others the benefit of the doubt before jumping to conclusions?

Al-Zamakhshari affirmed Mary's infallibility. Do you hold any lingering doubts or misconceptions about the purity of Maryam (peace be upon her) and the honor Allah gave her? What step will you take today to strengthen your respect for her station based on authentic sources?
